				<a href="/about" id="more-what-is">
				<h2>What is Next Nature?</h2>
				<p>With our attempts to cultivate nature, humankind causes the rising of a next nature, which is wild and unpredictable as ever. Wild systems, genetic surprises, autonomous machinery and splendidly beautiful black flowers. Nature changes along with us.</p>
				</a>
			</section>

			<li>
				<article id="post-44110">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/04/recreating-woolly-mammoth-dna/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="475" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2015/03/shutterstock_248386057-530x475.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="shutterstock_248386057" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/04/recreating-woolly-mammoth-dna/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Recreating Woolly Mammoth DNA">Recreating Woolly Mammoth DNA</a></h2>
					<p>Bioengineering might soon enable us to bring long gone animals back to life, <i>à la</i> <em>Jurassic Park</em>. Recently, a team of scientists at Harvard University managed to insert wooly mammoth DNA into the genome of its closest relative &#8211; the Asian elephant.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/04/recreating-woolly-mammoth-dna/#more-44110" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

			<li>
				<article id="post-42815">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/02/beautiful-wallpapers-created-with-vaccine/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="397" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/muniz_0001_Layer-5-530x397.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="muniz_0001_Layer-5" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/02/beautiful-wallpapers-created-with-vaccine/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Beautiful Wallpapers Created with Vaccine">Beautiful Wallpapers Created with Vaccine</a></h2>
					<p>Anti-vaccination movement is a hot topic these days. <a href="http://www.gatesfoundation.org/" target="_blank">Bill &amp; Melinda Gates Foundation</a> recently sponsored a series of artworks, named <a href="http://artofsavingalife.com/" target="_blank">The Art of Saving a Life</a>, in order to overcome the fear of vaccination. One of these artworks, called <a href="http://artofsavingalife.com/artists/vik-muniz/" target="_blank"><em></em><em>Flowers</em></a>, creates beautiful wallpapers out of smallpox vaccine.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/02/beautiful-wallpapers-created-with-vaccine/#more-42815" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

			<li>
				<article id="post-39618">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/05/scientists-created-alien-dna/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="396" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/dna-908e73761458dc9cc205d91bbca716ff2dbdd96a-s6-c30-530x396.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="dna-908e73761458dc9cc205d91bbca716ff2dbdd96a-s6-c30" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/05/scientists-created-alien-dna/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Scientists Created &#8220;Alien-DNA&#8221;">Scientists Created &#8220;Alien-DNA&#8221;</a></h2>
					<p>The genetic material of all creatures on earth is saved in the biomolecule Deoxyribonucleic Acid, the DNA. It consists of four components: the bases Adenin (A), Thymin (T), Guanin (G) and Cytosin (C). These appears as pairs in the combinations of AT and GC. Now, a team of scientists at the <a href="http://www.scripps.edu" target="_blank">Scripps Research Institute in California</a>, led by chemical biologist Floyd Romesberg, <a href="A semi-synthetic organism with an expanded genetic alphabet" target="_blank">extend the alphabet with two new created &#8216;foreign&#8217; building-blocks, called X and Y</a>. <span style="line-height: 1.5em;"> </span></p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/05/scientists-created-alien-dna/#more-39618" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

			<li>
				<article id="post-39518">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/05/stable-propagation-of-next-natural-dna/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="350" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/dna.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="Next Natural DNA" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/05/stable-propagation-of-next-natural-dna/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Stable Propagation of Next Natural DNA">Stable Propagation of Next Natural DNA</a></h2>
					<p>A team of American scientists created <a href="http://www.nature.com/nature/journal/vaop/ncurrent/full/nature13314.html" target="_blank">a semi-synthetic organism with an expanded genetic alphabet</a>. Old, natural DNA consists of two distinct base pairs, A-T and G-C. The letters refer to specific sub-units within a pair adenine (A) binds to thymine (T) and cytosine (C) binds to guanine (G) to create the well known double helix.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/05/stable-propagation-of-next-natural-dna/#more-39518" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/03/bugs-developed-immunity-to-gmo-corn/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Bugs Developed Immunity to GMO Corn">Bugs Developed Immunity to GMO Corn</a></h2>

			<li>
				<article id="post-38127">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/02/fish-fins-vs-bones/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="462" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/danio_rerio-530x7931.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="danio_rerio-530x793" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/02/fish-fins-vs-bones/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Fish Fins vs Bones">Fish Fins vs Bones</a></h2>
					<p>After investigating how to <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2012/05/regrowing-bones-with-silk/" target="_blank">regrow bones with silk</a>, biologists found out that zebrafish, a tropical fish native to the Himalayan region but very common in tanks, could be studied for the same purpose. In fact, this aquatic species has the amazing ability to regenerate lost appendages, such as fins.</p>
<p>Researchers at the <a href="http://uonews.uoregon.edu/archive/news-release/2014/1/zebra-fish-fins-help-oregon-researchers-gain-insight-bone-regeneration" target="_blank">University of Oregon</a> discovered that this process is applicable to human bones as well.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/02/fish-fins-vs-bones/#more-38127" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/01/all-natural-e-nemies/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="640" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/allnaturalblueberries-530x7491.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="allnaturalblueberries-530x749" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/01/all-natural-e-nemies/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to All-Natural E-nemies">All-Natural E-nemies</a></h2>
					<p>Chemistry teacher <a href="http://jameskennedymonash.files.wordpress.com/2014/01/ingredients-of-all-natural-blueberries-poster1.pdf" target="_blank">James Kennedy</a> sat down to show us that if we speak in terms of good and evil, Mother Nature&#8217;s products are far sneakier and complex than the lab&#8217;s. He virtually listed all the ingredients of non-GM fruits (excluding pesticides, fertilizers, insecticides or other contaminants), to reveal 13 E-numbers &#8220;naturally&#8221; packed in your morning blueberries, together with flavorings and fresh air.</p>

				<article id="post-37307">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/12/forward-to-the-dark-ages-our-horrifying-post-antibiotic-future/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="352" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/antibiotic-resistence--530x352.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="antibiotic resistence" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/12/forward-to-the-dark-ages-our-horrifying-post-antibiotic-future/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Forward to the Dark Ages: Our Horrifying Post-Antibiotic Future">Forward to the Dark Ages: Our Horrifying Post-Antibiotic Future</a></h2>
					<p>Before the 1940s, the most simple, everyday maladies – a bug bite, a broken bone, a sore throat – could result in swift and sudden death, cutting down people even in the prime of their lives. This was the era before antibiotics became a cornerstone of modern medicine. Now, thanks to overprescription of antibiotics, the massive overuse of antibiotics in factory-style farming, and stalled antibiotic research, we&#8217;re rapidly returning to the pre-penicillin era. Bacteria have evolved resistance to our best and, right now, our only, weapons.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/12/forward-to-the-dark-ages-our-horrifying-post-antibiotic-future/#more-37307" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

				<article id="post-36212">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/10/how-to-turn-skin-cells-into-a-baby/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="392" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/Screen-shot-2013-10-03-at-10.12.16-AM-530x392.png" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="thumb sucking human fetus" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/10/how-to-turn-skin-cells-into-a-baby/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to How to Turn Skin Cells into a Baby">How to Turn Skin Cells into a Baby</a></h2>
					<p>A Japanese biologist, Katsuhiko Hayashi, has managed to create both sperm and egg cells from stem cells in mice.  Not only that, but Hayashi was even able to produce a viable baby mouse using these same stem cells. His research may have far-reaching consequences for human fertility, one of which would be that two men or two women could make a biological baby together.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/10/how-to-turn-skin-cells-into-a-baby/#more-36212" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>

				<article id="post-36322">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/09/the-insect-with-natural-mechanical-gears/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="431" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2013/09/Gear1-530x431.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="Gear" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/09/the-insect-with-natural-mechanical-gears/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to The Insect with Natural Mechanical Gears">The Insect with Natural Mechanical Gears</a></h2>
					<p>At first glance the picture might look like the delicate gear wheel from an old Swiss watch, but it is actually the first and only mechanical gear ever found in nature. It belongs to a three-millimeter-long hopping insect, known as <em>Issus Coleoptratus</em>. The gears are located at the top of the insects’ hind legs and include 10 to 12 tapered teeth, allowing the insect to jump forward.<br />
 <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/09/the-insect-with-natural-mechanical-gears/#more-36322" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>

					<p><b>In the basement recording studio of the journal <i>Nature</i> scientist and broadcaster Adam Rutherford sat down with speculative architect Liam Young to discuss the mythical beasts of synthetic biology. Rutherford recently worked with the BBC on a series called the ‘Gene Code’ which explored the consequences of decoding the human genome. Recognizing the potential externalities of communicating science poorly, Rutherford works at conveying the poorly understood field of synthetic biology to a broader audience.</b></p>

			<li>
				<article id="post-35562">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/08/oranges-are-going-extinct-unless-a-gene-from-spinach-can-help/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="353" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/citrus-greening.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="citrus greening" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/08/oranges-are-going-extinct-unless-a-gene-from-spinach-can-help/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Oranges Are Going Extinct – Unless a Gene from Spinach Can Help">Oranges Are Going Extinct – Unless a Gene from Spinach Can Help</a></h2>
					<p>The apocalypse is on its way – at least for oranges. Citrus greening, a disease that kills citrus trees and makes their fruit green, shrunken and inedibly bitter, is racing across the globe. The disease, which is transmitted from tree to tree by a tiny insect called a psyllid, was first reported in China in 1943. Since then, it&#8217;s spread across the globe, finally making its way to Florida&#8217;s famous orange groves in 2005.</p>
<p>There is no known cure. A worldwide search failed to turn up a naturally immune tree. Measures like burning infected trees and dousing the psyllids with insecticide slow but do not stop the disease. With such seemingly bleak odds, does this mean the end of oranges, lemons and grapefruits?</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/08/oranges-are-going-extinct-unless-a-gene-from-spinach-can-help/#more-35562" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

			<li>
				<article id="post-35473">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/07/taste-the-artificial-fish-rainbow/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="353" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/discus-breed-fish-530x353.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="discus breed fish" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/07/taste-the-artificial-fish-rainbow/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Taste the Artificial Fish Rainbow">Taste the Artificial Fish Rainbow</a></h2>
					<p>A gorgeously uncanny school of discus fish cluster in an aquarium, all of them captive breeds. Though there&#8217;s nothing unusual about artificially selecting animals for <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2011/03/breeding-qr-codes/">flamboyant</a> or <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2011/06/blue-belgian-and-beefy/">bizarre</a> traits, it&#8217;s still compelling to see such a lovely display of manmade biodiversity. Some of these discus strains are the result of &#8220;natural&#8221; hybridization between fish from different geographic locations, while others are the result of <a href="http://www.aquaria.co.za/p_livestock_discus_strains.html">random mutations and intense inbreeding</a>.</p>
<p>Photo via <a href="http://www.practicalfishkeeping.co.uk/custom/images/medium/vazpb01vk.jpg">Practical Fish Keeping</a>.</p>
				</article>

										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/06/what-will-we-look-like-in-100000-years/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="337" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/100000-Years1_Feature-530x337.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="100000-Years1_Feature" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/06/what-will-we-look-like-in-100000-years/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to What Will We Look Like in 100,000 Years?">What Will We Look Like in 100,000 Years?</a></h2>
					<p>In 100,000 years human beings might look like a manga character: big intense eyes, high forehead, large head, straight nose, more pigmented skin, and perfect symmetry. <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/06/what-will-we-look-like-in-100000-years/#more-34589" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>

			<li>
				<article id="post-34281">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/06/purple-gm-tomatoes-prevent-cancer/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="351" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/purple-tomotoes--530x351.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="Scientists Engineer Cancer Fighting Purple Tomatoes" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/06/purple-gm-tomatoes-prevent-cancer/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Purple GM Tomatoes Prevent Cancer">Purple GM Tomatoes Prevent Cancer</a></h2>
					<p>Normally, when we select for characteristics in fruits and vegetables, it&#8217;s to bring them closer to some modernist ideal: corn that&#8217;s sweeter, lettuce that&#8217;s crisper, cucumbers that are <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2009/07/comeback-of-the-ugly-fruits/">perfectly green and straight</a>. However, a new strain of tomato out of the UK may soon topple the <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2007/08/dutch-tomatoes/">spherical red fruit</a> from its iconic position. These purple GM tomatoes owe their unusual hue to a dark purple-blue pigment called anthocynanin. Not only does this antioxidant double the shelf life of tomatoes in the supermarkt, it also extends the lives of mice that are genetically predisposed to cancer. A tomato that cuts down on food waste and the incidence of cancer? Even if pasta and pizza will never look the same, maybe it&#8217;s time to pass the purple.</p>
<p>Via <a href="http://news.jic.ac.uk/2013/05/purple-tomatoes/">John Innes Centre</a>. Photo via <a href="http://www.naturaleater.com/press-articles/Press-Purple-tomatoes.htm">Natural Eater</a>.<br />
Thanks to Peter Klomp for the heads up!</p>
				</article>

			<li>
				<article id="post-33379">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/05/modifying-milk-and-glowing-livestock/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="326" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2013/04/glowing_sheep-530x326.png" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="genetically modified sheep" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/05/modifying-milk-and-glowing-livestock/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Modifying Milk and Glowing Livestock">Modifying Milk and Glowing Livestock</a></h2>
					<p>A team of scientists from the Animal Reproduction Institute of Uruguay have genetically modified nine sheep with a phosphorescent jellyfish protein. This causes the lambs to grow a neon green colour when exposed to ultraviolet light. Besides the lambs&#8217; predisposition to glow green, they are otherwise perfectly healthy and normal.</p>
<p>Genetically modifying the sheep to glow under UV light is an attempt to advance and perfect the technique that will allow scientists to add beneficial new genes to livestock. Once the genes are integrated into an animal&#8217;s DNA, it can produce milk with various medical advantages for humans. Perhaps this could lead to the creation of a real-life <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korova_Milk_Bar" target="_blank">Korova Milk Bar</a>, the bar from &#8220;A Clockwork Orange&#8221; that offers drug-laced milk.</p>
<p>Story via <a href="http://www.redorbit.com/news/science/1112832841/glow-in-the-dark-sheep-altered-with-jellyfish-protein-042913/" target="_blank">redorbit</a>. Image via Fundación IRAUy / J. Calvelo</p>
				</article>

			<li>
				<article id="post-31567">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/03/artist-creates-portraits-of-strangers-using-dna-in-discarded-hair/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="233" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2013/02/DNAfaces08-530x233.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="DNAfaces08" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/03/artist-creates-portraits-of-strangers-using-dna-in-discarded-hair/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Artist Creates Portraits of Strangers Using DNA in Discarded Hair">Artist Creates Portraits of Strangers Using DNA in Discarded Hair</a></h2>
					<p>Through cigarette butts and strands of loose hair, we constantly and carelessly discard our genetic material. One New York-based artist, Heather Dewey-Hagborg, used these random traces left behind by unsuspecting strangers to make sculptures of what their owners might look like.</p>
<p>In her <em>Stranger Visions </em>series, Dewey-Hagborg created physical models using DNA facial modeling software and a 3D printer. The masks reflect eye color, geographical roots, sex, and other traits, but not exact facial features because forensic phenotyping can’t yet fill in all the details. <em>Stranger Visions</em> calls attention to the potential for a culture of &#8220;genetic surveillance&#8221; made possible by inexpensive $1,000 DNA sequencers. “As a society,&#8221; says Dewey-Hagborg, &#8221;we need to have a discussion about that.”</p>
<p>Soon, our entire genome may be accessible to strangers within minutes, with fears of cloning or genetic hacking to go along with it. It&#8217;s unsettling to think that our DNA, and therefore our identities, are not as precious as we think they are.</p>
<p>Via <a href="http://www.designboom.com/technology/heather-dewey-hagborg-creates-3d-portraits-using-dna/">Designboom</a>.</p>
				</article>

				<article id="post-31141">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/02/implanted-into-bacteria-synthetic-dna-functions-as-a-diagnostic-computer/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="297" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2013/02/627-530x297.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="627" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/02/implanted-into-bacteria-synthetic-dna-functions-as-a-diagnostic-computer/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Implanted into Bacteria, Synthetic DNA Functions as a Diagnostic Computer">Implanted into Bacteria, Synthetic DNA Functions as a Diagnostic Computer</a></h2>
					<p>In the movie Fantastic Voyage, a submarine and its crew were shrunk and injected into the body of a sick man in an attempt to save his life. Despite the fictional nature of this story, in the near future miniaturized, organic &#8220;computers&#8221; may roam our bodies, detecting early-stage diseases and treating them on the spot. There are already 10 times more bacterial cells than human cells in our bodies – so why not add a few more?</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/02/implanted-into-bacteria-synthetic-dna-functions-as-a-diagnostic-computer/#more-31141" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>
